  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_934e50ae-b10e-48c3-999f-b381e64a4e38'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer8360631805448078009">Christopher Snow is different from all the other residents of Moonlight Bay, different from anyone you've ever met. For Christopher Snow has made his peace with a very rare genetic disorder shared by only one thousand other Americans, a disorder that leaves him dangerously vulnerable to light. His life is filled with the fascinating rituals of one who must embrace the dark</span>
  <span id="freeText8360631805448078009" style="display:none">Christopher Snow is different from all the other residents of Moonlight Bay, different from anyone you've ever met. For Christopher Snow has made his peace with a very rare genetic disorder shared by only one thousand other Americans, a disorder that leaves him dangerously vulnerable to light. His life is filled with the fascinating rituals of one who must embrace the dark. He knows the night as no one else ever will, ever can - the mystery, the beauty, the many terrors, and the eerie, silken rhythms of the night - for it is only at night that he is free. Until the night he witnesses a series of disturbing incidents that sweep him into a violent mystery only he can solve, a mystery that will force him to rise above all fears and confront the many-layered strangeness of Moonlight Bay and its residents.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">You are referring to the Odd Thomas series. Oddie is loved by thousands, maybe millions, of folks. My favourite book in the series is the one spent in<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">You are referring to the Odd Thomas series. Oddie is loved by thousands, maybe millions, of folks. My favourite book in the series is the one spent in a monastery, Brother Odd, I like Odd, but my all-time favourite Koontz character has to be Christopher Snow of the Moonlight Bay series. In fact as an ensemble, there is no better group of faithful friends and comrades in Koontzland than Christopher Snow, Orson, Sasha, Bobby, Roosevelt Frost and Mungojerry. (Koontz loves dogs, especially golden retrievers but after reading the Christopher Snow (Moonlight Bay) series, I just have to yell “Hurray for the cat”!)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2517658972" />
    <a title="Obsidian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35942740-obsidian"><img alt="Obsidian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509845837p2/35942740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2517658972?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Obsidian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Obsidian" href="/user/show/35942740-obsidian">Obsidian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6701884-fear-nothing">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35942740-obsidian?shelf=2018-library-books">2018-library-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35942740-obsidian?shelf=halloween-bingo-2018">halloween-bingo-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2517658972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4610136133311856392">I usually like to wait a bit before posting a review. However, I just want to be done with this terrible book. I cannot with how slow and boring it was and how there was no development to any character we meet! At one point I was having a flashback to another Koontz book where there is a super dog, a man and woman, and an other thing that wanted to kill the dog. No I don't care what book I am thinking of, I am just writing that to prove the point that Koontz repeats himself. In addition this who</span>
  <span id="freeText4610136133311856392" style="display:none">I usually like to wait a bit before posting a review. However, I just want to be done with this terrible book. I cannot with how slow and boring it was and how there was no development to any character we meet! At one point I was having a flashback to another Koontz book where there is a super dog, a man and woman, and an other thing that wanted to kill the dog. No I don't care what book I am thinking of, I am just writing that to prove the point that Koontz repeats himself. In addition this whole book is like a prelude to the Odd Thomas series. Christopher Snow acts like Odd Thomas's long lost brother in so many ways I kept getting confused. The ending was a joke. I know there is a second book in this series, well too bad, I have no intention of reading it. <br /><br />"Fear Nothing" had an interesting premise. A young man who has a rare genetic disorder cannot be out in the sunlight. He has lived his life at night and under the moon. He somehow has a super hot girlfriend who is a deejay, and also knows her way around guns (like most female characters in Koontz's books). He has a cool dog named Orson and apparently parents who loved him. He also has a best friend who is a surfer that talks like he's in his 50s though he is the same age as Christopher (late 20s).<br /><br /> Koontz pitches you into something dark and nasty right away when we find out that Christopher's father is dying and he goes to the hospital to be there when he passes away. Apparently his father dying was the last thing keeping things in the community of Moonlight Bay together. After Christopher witnesses people stealing his father's body, he is on the run for his life and hiding from long time friends he has known since he was a boy. <br /><br />There are also monkeys. Sigh. <br /><br />Christopher is Odd Thomas and Odd Thomas is Christopher. Not quite a Gary Sue here, but pretty freaking close. He talks in metaphors and similes and made me wish for his character's death. He also is Too Stupid to Live (TSTL) as shown by him running from place to place and not telling anyone what is going on. when he does talk to his girlfriend, Sasha, he doesn't tell her what's going on for plot reasons. <br /><br />He does have a break and go to his best friend's house where surfer talk reigns and where I once again hoped for the death of both of these characters.<br /><br />The secondary characters are merely there to prop up Christopher or throw some random saying at him.<br /><br />Christopher's girlfriend is just there. She has no personality at all besides she's a deejay and she loves Christopher and calls him Snowman. The dog had more of a personality than she did.<br /><br />Christopher's best friend Bobby is kind of a jerk. He doesn't like to listen to unpleasant things and just tells Christopher to forget about things. And then randomly throws out how his estranged girlfriend thinks she's the reincarnation of an Hawaiian goddess. And maybe he is a god. I don't know. My brain shut off at that point and watched a British baking show which I am now obsessed with. <br /><br />There are multiple bad guys and evil animals and it was just not very well done. We had one character talk about raping his granddaughter and my bile rose up. This didn't make it horror, just something unpleasant that was trying too hard. <br /><br />The why behind all of this is beyond stupid. I could not with the reveal. <br /><br />The writing is late in his career Koontz. There just seems to be pointless dialogue between characters and them people running. There is a gunfight in the end and I maybe laughed cause the whole thing was peak absurd.<br /><br />The flow was awful. This was a struggle to keep reading and to stay on top of while I was reading too. <br /><br />The setting of Moonlight Bay must have only 20 people that live there since that is all who seemed to make up this book. <br /><br />The ending was a hot mess. Not really an ending and I am guessing using to set up book #2 which is "Seize the Night."</span>
  <a data-text-id="4610136133311856392" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2447817902" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2447817902" />
    <a title="Cody | CodysBookshelf" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf"><img alt="Cody | CodysBookshelf" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592500568p2/56352820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2447817902?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cody | CodysBookshelf" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cody | CodysBookshelf" href="/user/show/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf">Cody | CodysBookshelf</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553106640" href="/book/show/492572.Fear_Nothing">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf?shelf=dean-koontz">dean-koontz</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2447817902" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13883077874229017940">This is a Dean Koontz novel. You know what you’re going to get.<br/><br/>Some wonky science gone horribly wrong. Conspiracies. Government involvement. A smart dog. A preachy protagonist. The Koontzian equivalent of a manic pixie girl (who is, of course, deeply and madly in love with the protagonist). <br/><br/>Yeah, <i>Fear Nothing</i> is one of those quintessential Koontz books: pretty by-the-numbers stuff, but still fun.<br/><br/>Something I appreciated is the reference to <i>Watchers</i>; the goings on in Moonlight Bay are explained as</span>
  <span id="freeText13883077874229017940" style="display:none">This is a Dean Koontz novel. You know what you’re going to get.<br /><br />Some wonky science gone horribly wrong. Conspiracies. Government involvement. A smart dog. A preachy protagonist. The Koontzian equivalent of a manic pixie girl (who is, of course, deeply and madly in love with the protagonist). <br /><br />Yeah, <i>Fear Nothing</i> is one of those quintessential Koontz books: pretty by-the-numbers stuff, but still fun.<br /><br />Something I appreciated is the reference to <i>Watchers</i>; the goings on in Moonlight Bay are explained as an “improvement upon” the scientific discoveries from Koontz’s most famous work. This author does not typically reference himself, but in this case it worked. It made the book feel not quite so derivative. <br /><br /><i>Fear Nothing</i> is just plain fun. I couldn’t stop reading; I had to figure out the mysteries. Cheesy surfer lingo aside (in fact, most of the dialogue in this book is painfully cheesy and overwritten), this is a relatively solid adventure. Recommended for established Koontz fans, or anyone looking for a breezy summer read! </span>
  <a data-text-id="13883077874229017940" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_419736965" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/419736965" />
    <a title="Jane Stewart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart"><img alt="Jane Stewart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346001994p2/3789528.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/419736965?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jane Stewart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jane Stewart" href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart">Jane Stewart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio 9780739334300" href="/book/show/9821914-fear-nothing">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3789528-jane-stewart?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer419736965" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13662746535738546367">Too weird. No good story underneath. Events not supported. Lots of threats. Things not explained.<br/><br/>Most of the story takes place during two nights. Chris visits several people. There are long, vague, incomplete conversations with each person. There is a conspiracy/mystery and Chris is trying to figure out what is going on. Most people tell him things like “stop investigating. If you know too much you will regret it. The end of the world as we know it has begun.” A couple of people are angry and ac</span>
  <span id="freeText13662746535738546367" style="display:none">Too weird. No good story underneath. Events not supported. Lots of threats. Things not explained.<br /><br />Most of the story takes place during two nights. Chris visits several people. There are long, vague, incomplete conversations with each person. There is a conspiracy/mystery and Chris is trying to figure out what is going on. Most people tell him things like “stop investigating. If you know too much you will regret it. The end of the world as we know it has begun.” A couple of people are angry and accusing toward Chris saying “You are responsible for this.” Most people know things, but they won’t tell Chris. Instead they say “you shouldn’t know all of it, just enough to forget what you saw.” There is a tell all at the end where Chris finds answers in a letter. I did not enjoy it. I felt like I was watching the author’s dreams.<br /><br />Here’s an example of Chris visiting Roosevelt, a friend. Roosevelt knows what is going on but he won’t tell Chris. Instead it’s a long scene with Roosevelt talking to Chris’ dog Orson and talking about other pets and animals. Finally at the end of the scene, Roosevelt tells Chris that he must not ask any more questions or “they” will kill Chris’ friends, but “they” are not interested in killing Chris. He won’t give any more details.<br /><br />Too many things are not explained, for example: Why some revered Chris and were in awe of him and wouldn’t kill him. Why wouldn’t people tell Chris the whole story? What happened and why with the hitchhiker. The title of the book didn’t make sense. Those were the dad’s last words to Chris. I wanted more details about why and what happened to the dad. Why Chris’ friendship with Manuel is now over. Why did Orson hate Chris temporarily three years ago. What was the cause and motive for Chris’ mother’s death? What are the motives for why some monkeys are killing humans. What’s the deal with dolls that looked like Chris? I wanted to know more about the leader of the monkeys? How did that work? How did that start?<br /><br />What I liked: Chris had a genetic disorder. He will develop skin cancer and eye cancer from light bulbs and the sun. It’s almost a miracle that he’s lived to age 28. He knows he doesn’t have a long life ahead. I liked his attitude about living. After a major crisis that almost killed Chris and his friends, a friend asked “what do we do now?” Chris said “get a beer.” She said “after that?” Chris said “Can’t drink beer forever. Catch a wave.” Although he’s carrying a gun (for the first time in his life) he’s not worrying about things. It’s calming to see his attitude.<br /><br />The narrator Keith Szarabajka was excellent. I’d be interested in another book just for his narration. At times his voice is gravelly and low. I really liked listening to him.<br /><br />DATA:<br />Narrative mode: 1st person Chris. Unabridged audiobook reading time: 12 hrs and 37 mins. Swearing language: strong including religious swear words, but not often. Sexual language: none. Number of sex scenes: one referred to, no details. Setting: around 1998 Moonlight Bay, California. Book copyright: 1998. Genre: mystery suspense. Ending: good for now.<br /><br /><br />OTHER BOOKS:<br />For a list of my reviews of other Dean Koontz books, see my 5 star review of Lightning<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/356619614">http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/...</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13662746535738546367" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_821781909" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/821781909" />
    <a title="Corielle Hayley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5220114-corielle-hayley"><img alt="Corielle Hayley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350792671p2/5220114.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/821781909?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Corielle Hayley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Corielle Hayley" href="/user/show/5220114-corielle-hayley">Corielle Hayley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5220114-corielle-hayley?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer821781909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1403044005151266575">“Never leave a friend behind. Friends are all we have to get us through this life–and they are the only things from this world that we could hope to see in the next.”<br/><br/>I love this book. I really do. I’m not certain why, really. Dean Koontz is a schmaltzy writer. He overuses analogies and some of them are rather bizarre. Many of his books have similar details — bad ass chicks, unlikely heroes, a golden retriever or two. They start to blur together after a while. But when I was in middle school and </span>
  <span id="freeText1403044005151266575" style="display:none">“Never leave a friend behind. Friends are all we have to get us through this life–and they are the only things from this world that we could hope to see in the next.”<br /><br />I love this book. I really do. I’m not certain why, really. Dean Koontz is a schmaltzy writer. He overuses analogies and some of them are rather bizarre. Many of his books have similar details — bad ass chicks, unlikely heroes, a golden retriever or two. They start to blur together after a while. But when I was in middle school and high school, I read every single thing Koontz had published. This book (and its sequel, Seize the Night) always seemed to stand out. I reread it every few years, and I’ve also listened to the audiobook a few times. This time was the audiobook, mostly at the gym. It’s just a good, solid story with a very likable lead (and a black lab).<br /><br />Fear Nothing is about a 28 year old man named Chris Snow. I am now 28. I think I read this book for the first time when I was 12. I feel old. Chris suffers from a condition called xeroderma pigmentosum (XP) that prevents his cells from being able to repair themselves after exposure to light. As a result, he has lived his life in a dimly lit house during the day. At night, he explores the small town of Midnight Bay, where he lives.<br /><br />This novel begins in the evening, as Chris gets a phone call that his father has passed away from cancer. A fluke event at the hospital leads Chris to see someone do something strange with his father’s remains. He investigates, and stumbles upon a mystery that affects his whole town. I don’t want to spoil anything, but I’ll say one thing: genetically modified monkeys. Yeah, that’s right.<br /><br />The events of the novel take place primarily over a 24 hour period, as Chris explores his town and visits friends and enemies, trying to find the truth about his father’s death. I think one of the things I loved so much about this novel was the romantic idea of having a whole town to yourself in the dark; just you, your dog and your bicycle.<br /><br />Fear Nothing ends abruptly, with few questions answered. Koontz published a sequel, Seize the Night, the following year. Supposedly he’s working on a third. 13 year old me can’t wait.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1403044005151266575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_132375589" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132375589" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132375589?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dustin Crazy little brown owl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dustin Crazy little brown owl" href="/user/show/2454496-dustin-crazy-little-brown-owl">Dustin Crazy little brown owl</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553106640" href="/book/show/492572.Fear_Nothing">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132375589" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer684332427845717469">It's easy to see why Christopher Snow of Moonlight Bay has such a fan following. The story and dialogue is entertaining and the writing is intriguingly executed. Dean Koontz Addicts continue to hold out hope for book three, Ride The Storm, to be completed and published even though it's been 20 years since the journey began. <br/><br/>This series is recommended for readers who are interested in venturing into the mysterious threshold of alternate realities.<br/><br/>Some Favorite Passages:<br/><i><br/>He was great because he was</i></span>
  <span id="freeText684332427845717469" style="display:none">It's easy to see why Christopher Snow of Moonlight Bay has such a fan following. The story and dialogue is entertaining and the writing is intriguingly executed. Dean Koontz Addicts continue to hold out hope for book three, Ride The Storm, to be completed and published even though it's been 20 years since the journey began. <br /><br />This series is recommended for readers who are interested in venturing into the mysterious threshold of alternate realities.<br /><br />Some Favorite Passages:<br /><i><br />He was great because he was kind. He was great because he was humble, gentle, full of laughter.<br /><br />So many thoughtless people have made unkind assumptions about me, based on my appearance and my affinity for the night, that I am reluctant to join the club of cruelty and speak ill of anyone without ample reason.<br /><br />A sense of unreality overcame me - that I should find myself in these strange circumstances. I could almost believe that I had somehow fallen into a dream without first falling asleep.<br /><br />I felt wonderful, really wonderful. It was the last time I ever felt wonderful - and the last time I ever will.<br /><br />Like blood out of a wound, silence welled up from the bottom of the house into this upstairs hall.<br /><br />I stopped chasing ghosts and reluctantly returned to the upstairs hallway. A doll was waiting for me.<br /><br />This narrow, life-sustaining realm under the smoke seemed to be an alternate world into which I had fallen after stepping through a door between dimensions.<br /><br />An inhuman cry issued from him, primitive and psychotic, a caterwaul of the sort that sometimes wakes you in the night and leaves you wondering about the species of origin.<br /><br />"And they left me a warning," Bobby said.<br />I pictured a threatening note laboriously printed in crude block letters - WATCH YOUR ASS. Signed, THE MONKEYS.<br />They were too clever to leave a paper trail, however, and even more direct. Bobby said, "One of them crapped on my bed."<br /><br />"The first big hurdle is believing you can actually do it. Putting aside your doubt, your cynicism, all your preconceived notions about what's possible and what isn't. Most of all, hardest of all, you have to stop worrying about looking foolish, 'cause fear of being humiliated really limits you. Lots of folks could never get past all that, and I'm sort of surprised that I got past it myself."<br /><br />"Sir," I told him, "I take back what I said earlier. After careful consideration, I've decided you're totally awesomely crazy, whacked-out to the max."<br /><br />As Roosevelt settled into his chair again, my bewilderment began to give way to a tremulous sense of the miraculous. I am aware of a looming revelation that would rock my life forever, expose dimensions of the world that I could not now imagine; but although I strained to grasp it, this understanding remained elusive, tantalizing just beyond the limits of my reach.<br /><br />"But these new cats I've been encountering the last two years or so . . . they open a far more exciting dimension of communication."<br /><br />"They have their own agenda. Maybe sometimes it matches ours. They don't want the world to know about this, either. Their future isn't in undoing what's been done. Their future is the new world coming."</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="684332427845717469" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Lynda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2798768-lynda"><img alt="Lynda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426871680p2/2798768.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/73210047?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lynda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lynda" href="/user/show/2798768-lynda">Lynda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2798768-lynda?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer73210047" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16992486731905244643">Christopher Snow lives in the sleepy little town of Moonlight Bay. He has a rare disease called XP which prevents him from getting any sunlight or being in bright light at all. His body doesn’t repair ultra-violet damage the way most bodies do. Therefore Christopher is resigned to live his life by the night and he knows just about every inch of Moonlight Bay.<br/><br/>His girlfriend Sasha and his boyhood friend Bobby are his closest companions and they both love him dearly and would do anything for him.<br/><br/>He</span>
  <span id="freeText16992486731905244643" style="display:none">Christopher Snow lives in the sleepy little town of Moonlight Bay. He has a rare disease called XP which prevents him from getting any sunlight or being in bright light at all. His body doesn’t repair ultra-violet damage the way most bodies do. Therefore Christopher is resigned to live his life by the night and he knows just about every inch of Moonlight Bay.<br /><br />His girlfriend Sasha and his boyhood friend Bobby are his closest companions and they both love him dearly and would do anything for him.<br /><br />He lives with his dog, Orson, who almost seems to be able to understand what you’re saying and respond.<br /><br />On this night, Christopher Snow’s father, who is afflicted with cancer, dies. Chris makes a rare venture out into the world of light to go to the hospital to see his father one last time before he dies. After he’s gone and the body is taken to be cremated, Chris remembers his father wants to be cremated with a picture of Chris’s mother who died two years ago in a car accident. He rushes down to the basement to catch up with the men who took the body, but instead he finds an odd scene. A man in a van brought another body of a dead hitchhiker to be swapped out with Chris’s dad. Apparently someone wants to do more tests on Chris’s father.<br /><br />This is the beginning of a strange night full of events for Chris Snow which leads him to discover a frightening military experiment has been going on in Moonlight Bay for years. It’s the end of the world as we know it and it’s too late to stop what’s already happened.<br /><br />What’s worse, Chris’s mother was involved in the whole thing and as it turns out, she may have been murdered or killed herself.<br /><br />Chris tries to find the truth in amid all the lies and secrets. He risks his life and his friends’ lives in this pursuit.<br /><br />The ‘frightening experiment’ involves gene splicing which will allow superior intelligence. It has been tested on a variety of animals and in the first batch, although they exhibited superior intelligence, they also exhibited massive violence and hatred.<br /><br />This book reminded me too much of Watchers and it even refers to The Francis Project that was behind all the happenings in Watchers. The difference is that this book didn’t have any of the heart that Watchers had. It was well written and suspenseful, but in the end, I didn’t really care about any of the characters. Orson didn’t win me over as much as Einstein. And the violent creatures resulting in the experiment didn’t have the heart that The Outsider was known to have.<br /><br />Overall, this was a big let down. There’s another book with the same characters, but they didn’t win me over enough to want to read more about them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16992486731905244643" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/4694388?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17724829606495513792">I picked up this book at the airport when I came dangerously close to finishing my current book (The Unthiknable Thoughts of Jacob Green) before my 4 hour flight back to Chicago from LA. It was the best choice they had. I anticipate a mediocre reaction to this book. I like Koontz, but a lot of his books seem to be too similar for me.<br/><br/>---<br/>Despite not being a big fan of the 'formula novel' - you know, all those books that authors constantly crank out and end up on the top of the NYT bestseller's lis</span>
  <span id="freeText17724829606495513792" style="display:none">I picked up this book at the airport when I came dangerously close to finishing my current book (The Unthiknable Thoughts of Jacob Green) before my 4 hour flight back to Chicago from LA. It was the best choice they had. I anticipate a mediocre reaction to this book. I like Koontz, but a lot of his books seem to be too similar for me.<br /><br />---<br />Despite not being a big fan of the 'formula novel' - you know, all those books that authors constantly crank out and end up on the top of the NYT bestseller's list - I have to say that I enjoyed this book. I haven't really happened upon an engrossing read yet this year, but this book turned out to be one that had me longing to pick it up again. As with other Koontz novels, this book was a psychological thriller with a supernatural twist. Although engaging, I'm looking forward to reading something a bit 'meatier' from a more obscure author.</span>

<div id="review_88316898" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/88316898" />
    <a title="Maciek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2969647-maciek"><img alt="Maciek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1280839159p2/2969647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/88316898?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maciek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maciek" href="/user/show/2969647-maciek">Maciek</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780747258322" href="/book/show/959386.Fear_Nothing">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=own-in-hardcover">own-in-hardcover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=own-in-paperback">own-in-paperback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2969647-maciek?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer88316898" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1427550390652344402"><i>Fear Nothing</i> introduces Christopher Snow, a 20-something surfer who suffers from Xeroderma Pigmentosum - he can't go out during the day, as light is deadly for him. All light. Chris lives by candles, and by night.<br/><br/>Dean Koontz has the skill to write books that sustain the suspense and deliver engaging action, but he fails to do both with this one. The novel is narrated in the 1st person, a technique Koontz employed for the first time in <i>Twilight Eyes</i>, back in 1987. Sine the main character is a sur</span>
  <span id="freeText1427550390652344402" style="display:none"><i>Fear Nothing</i> introduces Christopher Snow, a 20-something surfer who suffers from Xeroderma Pigmentosum - he can't go out during the day, as light is deadly for him. All light. Chris lives by candles, and by night.<br /><br />Dean Koontz has the skill to write books that sustain the suspense and deliver engaging action, but he fails to do both with this one. The novel is narrated in the 1st person, a technique Koontz employed for the first time in <i>Twilight Eyes</i>, back in 1987. Sine the main character is a surfer, he and his friends speak only in surfer lingo, because that's how cool guys must talk right? To make matters worse, Koontz actually <i>explains</i> the lingo to the reader. I guess he truly does think that his readers are too stupid to understand slang, but for some reasons use words like "susurration" or "caterwaul" in their daily speech.<br /><br />The characters are cartoonish. Snow has nothing better to do than to go on and have adventures with his beautiful and perfect girlfriend who must be the next incarnation of Venus. His friend, Bobby, is a multimilionaire who drinks Heineken and has nothing better to do and go on adventures.<br /><br />Still, there's a pleasant story there. A small, quiet town haunted by the secrets of its inhabitants. It's been done multiple times before, both by Koontz and other writers, but it is a good frame for a story. Still, in this particular work Koontz tries to show off with some of the most self-indulgent, embarassing and overblown prose style since the Victorian novel. When one word is enough, he'll use twenty; he never misses an occasion to sidetrack the action with pointless detail and draw out the narrative to the extreme. The musing of the hero are not enlightening nor interesting; the descriptions that were the key points of his novels are inflated and pompuous beyond belief. This work is the antithesis of <i>Intensity</i>, which is propably Koontz's best novel. It foreshadows the terrible gradiloquent monsters that Koontz will write in years to come. This marks the end of his tight, entertaining thrillers.<br /><br />Still, even though Koontz is completely inept at telling the story he somehow succeeds at creating an eerie mood, even if he interrupts it with lame jokes and platitudes. <i>Fear Nothing</i> shares a lot of similarities with his earlier novel, <i>Midnight</i>, yet the fact is never brought up. <br /><i>Fear Nothing</i> contains a good story that screams for a good teller; unfortunately it suffers from too many of Koontz's literary abuses to be properly enjoyed.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1427550390652344402" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2918599967847465742">AWESOME! This book grabs you from the beginning and pulls you through a page turning adventure.   <span id="freeText2918599967847465742" style="display:none">AWESOME! This book grabs you from the beginning and pulls you through a page turning adventure. I starting the follow-up book as soon as I finished this one. More on that one later.<br /><br /><b>Publisher's Summary</b><br /><br />Christopher Snow is the best-known resident of 12,000-strong Moonlight Bay, California. This is because 28-year-old Chris has xeroderma pigmentosum (XP), a light-sensitivity so severe that he cannot leave his house in daylight, cannot enter a normally-lit room, cannot sit at a computer. Chris' natural element is the night, and his parents, both academics, chose to live in Moonlight Bay because in a small town Chris can make the nightscape his own, roaming freely through the town on his bike, surfing in the moonlight, exploring while most people sleep.<br /><br />But Chris' brilliant mother, a scientist, was killed in a car accident two years ago, and as the book opens his father, Steven Snow, is dying of cancer; Chris' protected life is about to change forever. We meet Chris as he is carefully preparing himself to go out in the late-afternoon sun to visit the hospital. In his last moments of life his father tells Chris he is sorry and that Chris should fear nothing, cryptic words that Chris cannot really relate to.<br /><br />Steven Snow's body is removed to the hospital basement for transport to the funeral home/crematorium, and when Chris goes downstairs for a final moment of farewell, he witnesses a frightening and clandestine encounter: the funeral director and another man Chris doesn't recognize are substituting the body of a hitchhiker for Steven Snow's body, which is being taken not to the crematorium but to some secret destination.<br /><br />For Chris, this scene is the first intimation of a conspiracy that he will come to realize envelopes many of his townspeople. His parents knew of it and wanted to protect Chris from it. His best friend has had hints of something wrong because of the frightening nocturnal visitors that have come to his beach house. And the first person to try to explain to Chris what's going on, and warn him about the special danger he himself is in, will be hideously murdered.</span>

<div id="review_2452090123" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2452090123" />
    <a title="The Face of Your Father" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/79119566-the-face-of-your-father"><img alt="The Face of Your Father" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597595315p2/79119566.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2452090123?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Face of Your Father" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Face of Your Father" href="/user/show/79119566-the-face-of-your-father">The Face of Your Father</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2452090123" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9592244243388510930">{Update on 10/11/2018 : I had to lower this to a 1.7. The more I think about it, the more I think it stinks..}<br/><br/>Dean Koontz’s ‘Fear Nothing’ is fun. In fact, it could be the most fun I’ve ever had while reading a Koontz problem. Yet … it all seems a bit formulaic, doesn’t it?<br/><br/>Christopher Snow has XP, a rare genetic disorder that makes it difficult for his skin to repair itself after being exposed to UV light. This makes it impossible for Chris to venture outside during the day as this can lead to f</span>
  <span id="freeText9592244243388510930" style="display:none">{Update on 10/11/2018 : I had to lower this to a 1.7. The more I think about it, the more I think it stinks..}<br /><br />Dean Koontz’s ‘Fear Nothing’ is fun. In fact, it could be the most fun I’ve ever had while reading a Koontz problem. Yet … it all seems a bit formulaic, doesn’t it?<br /><br />Christopher Snow has XP, a rare genetic disorder that makes it difficult for his skin to repair itself after being exposed to UV light. This makes it impossible for Chris to venture outside during the day as this can lead to fast developing melanomas. The citizens of Moonlight Bay know about Chris and Chris THOUGHT he knew his neighbors but after his father’s death, people begin to act very strangely.<br /><br />‘Fear Nothing’ displays Koontz’s superb ability to move a plot along. The story builds upon itself, gaining speed with each chapter. The entire 400 page novel takes place in a single night, this makes the story feel like an out of control freight train but maintains a well-organized structure by Koontz. In terms of character, there really is only one the reader can grab onto and that is the main protagonist, Christopher Snow. The concept of the vulnerable protagonist is expertly done by Koontz and adds a layer of danger to every adventure Snow takes on. <br /><br />As usual, Koontz loses points in terms of dialogue. It is horrid and unnatural. Surfer lingo that is immediately explained after its use is grating and repetitive. <br /><br />Also, the rehashing of themes and concepts hurts this novel’s originality. There are aspects of ‘Watchers’, ‘Lightning’, ‘Innocence’, and more; this goes back to the theory that Koontz keeps re-writing the same story and slapping on a different title.<br /><br />Overall, this is the most fun 3 star book that I’ve ever read. It is a solid claustrophobic adventure with great mystery and shocking twists and turns. Christopher Snow is a fantastic lead in my opinion but he is a diamond in an ocean of shards of glass. 3/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="9592244243388510930" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2460434532" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2460434532" />
    <a title="Coni (coni_reads or skingproject)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5542828-coni-coni-reads-or-skingproject"><img alt="Coni (coni_reads or skingproject)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460088830p2/5542828.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2460434532?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Coni (coni_reads or skingproject)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Coni (coni_reads or skingproject)" href="/user/show/5542828-coni-coni-reads-or-skingproject">Coni (coni_reads or skingproject)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345533302" href="/book/show/13154938-fear-nothing">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5542828-coni-coni-reads-or-skingproject?shelf=physical-book">physical-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5542828-coni-coni-reads-or-skingproject?shelf=readbetweendean">readbetweendean</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2460434532" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14117443768512999628">One of the people that I follow on Instagram wanted to read a marathon of Dean Koontz books from what is considered his best works and I decided to join along. This is my first Koontz read. I can see the appeal. It jumps right into the action almost immediately and doesn't slow down until the end.<br/><br/>I did not see a lot of story elements and plot points coming. If I was a regular reader of Koontz, I might expect it, but it was out of nowhere for me. I really enjoyed reading it because I kept thinkin</span>
  <span id="freeText14117443768512999628" style="display:none">One of the people that I follow on Instagram wanted to read a marathon of Dean Koontz books from what is considered his best works and I decided to join along. This is my first Koontz read. I can see the appeal. It jumps right into the action almost immediately and doesn't slow down until the end.<br /><br />I did not see a lot of story elements and plot points coming. If I was a regular reader of Koontz, I might expect it, but it was out of nowhere for me. I really enjoyed reading it because I kept thinking, "This book is insane!" <br /><br />One drawback was whenever Koontz would describe surf lingo or something similar it would take me out of the story. One of the main character's friends is a surfer so it would be fine for the friend to speak that way, but it was weird to have the surfer speak that way and then have the author explained what he was saying. I think we could have figured it out, if we didn't know. Also, I felt that everything that was explained was pretty common knowledge. I tried to give him the benefit of the doubt thinking that it might not have been common knowledge when this book was written in 1998, but I feel like it was.<br /><br />There really isn't an ending to this book. Some freaky stuff happens and then it calms down only slightly at the end. Between the government experiments, conspiracies, and non-ending, it really reminded me of an X-Files episode. I could also see this as a schlocky sci-fi movie that would be really fun to watch. Has any of his books been made into movies? After a Google search, I see there has been and I've seen none of them. Maybe I will someday.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14117443768512999628" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_893329387" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/893329387" />
    <a title="Benjamin Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4209082-benjamin-thomas"><img alt="Benjamin Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451660582p2/4209082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/893329387?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Benjamin Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Benjamin Thomas" href="/user/show/4209082-benjamin-thomas">Benjamin Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780553106640" href="/book/show/492572.Fear_Nothing">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4209082-benjamin-thomas?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer893329387" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11921057783168249430">Once again, Dean Koontz proves he is a hit or miss writer.<br/><br/>This first book of the so-called "Moonlight Bay" trilogy has an intriguing main character, (Christopher Snow), an interesting premise involving secret experimentation at an abandoned military base using retroviruses to enhance intelligence in animals, and a nice setting on the California coast. Unfortunately, it just never quite lived up to its promise. It seemed like every time my interest started to peak, the main character waltzed off </span>
  <span id="freeText11921057783168249430" style="display:none">Once again, Dean Koontz proves he is a hit or miss writer.<br /><br />This first book of the so-called "Moonlight Bay" trilogy has an intriguing main character, (Christopher Snow), an interesting premise involving secret experimentation at an abandoned military base using retroviruses to enhance intelligence in animals, and a nice setting on the California coast. Unfortunately, it just never quite lived up to its promise. It seemed like every time my interest started to peak, the main character waltzed off into several pages of introspection on his life and what it all means.<br /><br />Granted, Christopher Snow's life is unique in that he suffers from a rare genetic disorder that leaves him dangerously vulnerable to light. Consequently he lives by night; even too many candles in a room make him squint. That's a great concept for a character but the plot wandered about quite a bit before settling on the obvious telegraphed path that had to unfold eventually. This one was close to earning only two stars from me except for some nice scenes with Christopher's best friend, Bobby, (a surfer dude), and a pretty cool fight with monkeys at the end. Monkeys, especially monkeys with heightened intelligence and an evil streak always make for great horror fiction.<br /><br />It seems even Koontz has abandoned this trilogy since the second book was published in 1999 and nothing since. Reportedly, Koontz had said in 2000 that he was half way through book 3 at that time. Hmmm...</span>
  <a data-text-id="11921057783168249430" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer428692411" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5687349663597153149">Christopher Snow has a rare condition called Xeroderma pigmentosum which prevents his body from repairing the damage done by uv light from the sun, light bulbs, etc., so he is a person of the night. Accompanied by his dog Orson, girlfriend Sasha and friend Bobby, he accidentally uncovers a secret from an apparently abandoned military base in Moonlight Bay. As he attempts to learn more about it, he and his friends are met with increasing amounts of threats and violence. <br/><br/>I reread this as a botm fo</span>
  <span id="freeText5687349663597153149" style="display:none">Christopher Snow has a rare condition called Xeroderma pigmentosum which prevents his body from repairing the damage done by uv light from the sun, light bulbs, etc., so he is a person of the night. Accompanied by his dog Orson, girlfriend Sasha and friend Bobby, he accidentally uncovers a secret from an apparently abandoned military base in Moonlight Bay. As he attempts to learn more about it, he and his friends are met with increasing amounts of threats and violence. <br /><br />I reread this as a botm for the Koontzland Goodreads group in Dec 2012. It was still entertaining to read again but I found many of the pages tedious and hard to keep reading as I didn't find it contributing to the story. The ending was disappointing as it felt rushed since it wrapped up in just a few pages and it left the book feeling incomplete as it didn't answer many of the questions about other parts of the plot. <br />The plot has the same basic characters as some of Koontz's books - hero, intelligent dog and a child with a mental affliction.</span>

<div id="review_1067245318" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1067245318" />
    <a title="C.P. Cabaniss" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9656259-c-p-cabaniss"><img alt="C.P. Cabaniss" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468698183p2/9656259.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1067245318?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.P. Cabaniss" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.P. Cabaniss" href="/user/show/9656259-c-p-cabaniss">C.P. Cabaniss</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9656259-c-p-cabaniss?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9656259-c-p-cabaniss?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9656259-c-p-cabaniss?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9656259-c-p-cabaniss?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1067245318" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14878108977511900069"><blockquote>
  <b>"Although I wasn't trained for this work, there was no one but me to do the job."</b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>This quote really sums up almost every Dean Koontz protagonist, and Christopher Snow is no different. Although there is darkness and creepiness in this book, it is very inspiring. It gives hope, because no matter what is happening in the world, there is always something good out there. <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>"A lot of the time, reality is what you make it."</b>
</blockquote> <br/><br/>I don't know why I haven't read this book before, because it's one of the </span>
  <span id="freeText14878108977511900069" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>"Although I wasn't trained for this work, there was no one but me to do the job."</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />This quote really sums up almost every Dean Koontz protagonist, and Christopher Snow is no different. Although there is darkness and creepiness in this book, it is very inspiring. It gives hope, because no matter what is happening in the world, there is always something good out there. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>"A lot of the time, reality is what you make it."</b>
</blockquote> <br /><br />I don't know why I haven't read this book before, because it's one of the best Koontz novels that I've read. The characters are vivid, the storyline is creepy, and it has a beautiful message. Although Chris has a less than ideal life, he <i>lives</i>. Life isn't about what you're given, it's what you make it. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>"When a society erases its past, for whatever reason, it cannot have a future."</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />There isn't a lot that I can say about this book without giving away lots of the plot. If you like Koontz you will probably enjoy this. You spend most of your time in Chris Snow's head, following a trail that leads to creepier and creepier revelations. The writing is stunningly beautiful. Orson, Chris's dog companion, is fantastic. Sasha and Bobby are wonderful friends. <br /><br />Just read the book. Right now. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>"I believe in the possibility of miracles."</b>
</blockquote><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14878108977511900069" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

May be it was a case of "it's me, not you book"; but half-way through, I wasn't sure I would finish it - but I did. I think I found Christopher Snow too young for my taste, and expected another development entirely, may be something verging on the supernatural?</span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/9586211-fear-nothing">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3378114-t?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3378114-t?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128185644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11642998487129840108">This series astonished me back into reading. When I was much younger I was most peculiar, so I spent my days doing whatever it is that comes to mind: pounding <i>gumamela</i> flowers in my backyard to make bubbles, peering down this most curious hole in the ground (turned out to be our <i>pozo negro</i>, ick!), learning how to ride a bike (bruises and all), reading the telephone directory upside down, and more. When there is that much to do in 1998, how can I find the time to sit down and just be interested i</span>
  <span id="freeText11642998487129840108" style="display:none">This series astonished me back into reading. When I was much younger I was most peculiar, so I spent my days doing whatever it is that comes to mind: pounding <i>gumamela</i> flowers in my backyard to make bubbles, peering down this most curious hole in the ground (turned out to be our <i>pozo negro</i>, ick!), learning how to ride a bike (bruises and all), reading the telephone directory upside down, and more. When there is that much to do in 1998, how can I find the time to sit down and just be interested in stories? Even my mother got me busy doing cross stitching.<br /><br />But then as it was a year of doing what I want to do, when I saw <i>Fear Nothing</i> from across the room, I just had to have it. Coincidentally it was also my mother who brought this home for me from their office library, hoping to keep me still, for once. And wow. Just like that, I was back to reading, and reading and reading and reading.<br /><br />After all these years it's still one of my favourite books, that I looked everywhere for my own copy. Finally found one this year, and I am just over the moon. I've read better books of course, other more amazing stories that just simply leave me with no words. But this one. Ah, this one. You know the feeling you get when your body finally finds the right chair to sit on? This book is my whole damn couch. Thank you, Dean.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2081674275" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2081674275" />
    <a title="T.C. Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32797985-t-c-michael"><img alt="T.C. Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558582091p2/32797985.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2081674275?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="T.C. Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="T.C. Michael" href="/user/show/32797985-t-c-michael">T.C. Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2081674275" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3429136800185430730">This was an enjoyable book, particularly because I really like Christopher Snow and his nighttime adventures. His health condition, XP for short, makes him see very personable and realistic. Plus, for the most part, I like his personality.<br/><br/>I read Seize the Night, book 2, first because I didn't know it was a series until after I finished it. Comparing that book to Fear Nothing, I feel that the actual plot itself and the sense of adventure is a little bit better in Seize the Night, but I feel like </span>
  <span id="freeText3429136800185430730" style="display:none">This was an enjoyable book, particularly because I really like Christopher Snow and his nighttime adventures. His health condition, XP for short, makes him see very personable and realistic. Plus, for the most part, I like his personality.<br /><br />I read Seize the Night, book 2, first because I didn't know it was a series until after I finished it. Comparing that book to Fear Nothing, I feel that the actual plot itself and the sense of adventure is a little bit better in Seize the Night, but I feel like the reader really gets to know Christopher and his friends and love life better in Fear Nothing.<br /><br />A complaint that I have in this book that mirrors my feelings in Seize the Night is Bobbie's attitude or personality. I don't really care for it. For some reason, it just comes off as annoying and slightly shallow. Maybe it's the fact that he's super rich, got to drop out of school, and all he does all day is surf. He has a very laid back attitude about life and responsibility. In fact, he doesn't seem to have much responsibility either, besides his daily scan of the ocean waves.<br /><br />Another complaint is the way Dea Koontz wrote this book. I've read a few of his other books and maybe I'm just misremembering, but it seems like in this one he was very wordy. He used so many words to describe almost everything that it seemed like he over did it on the prose. This may be coming from my author side and not my reader side, but it felt like he could have cut back on the extra words by half and it still would have been a great book.<br /><br />Anyways, this was a good read and full of suspense and thrills. There were parts of the book where I was actually scared for Christopher's life. I definitely recommend this book to others who enjoy thrillers. (4/5)</span>
  <a data-text-id="3429136800185430730" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2390757692" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2390757692" />
    <a title="Charley Girl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12157066-charley-girl"><img alt="Charley Girl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378175527p2/12157066.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2390757692?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charley Girl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charley Girl" href="/user/show/12157066-charley-girl">Charley Girl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12157066-charley-girl?shelf=2018-read">2018-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2390757692" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11048189622743547980">Christopher Snow cannot handle light as in it will kill him. He wasn't expected to live long but somehow he is 28 and has experienced his mother's death and now his father's. His father's last words to Chris are, "Fear Nothing". <br/><br/>Chris sees people taking his father's body and the mystery begins. Why? He travels through the night with his best buddy, Orson to solve the mystery enlisting his childhood friend, Bobby, and girlfriend Sasha.<br/><br/>It is a creepy book but has underlying lessons in it. Friends </span>
  <span id="freeText11048189622743547980" style="display:none">Christopher Snow cannot handle light as in it will kill him. He wasn't expected to live long but somehow he is 28 and has experienced his mother's death and now his father's. His father's last words to Chris are, "Fear Nothing". <br /><br />Chris sees people taking his father's body and the mystery begins. Why? He travels through the night with his best buddy, Orson to solve the mystery enlisting his childhood friend, Bobby, and girlfriend Sasha.<br /><br />It is a creepy book but has underlying lessons in it. Friends are worth anything to keep, worrying about tomorrow lessens your enjoyment of today and there is always something good in your life, so enjoy it. <br /><br />On to the second book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11048189622743547980" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/156550984?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Louize" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Louize" href="/user/show/3019973-louize">Louize</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156550984" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2854479971610080366"><br/><i>
  <b>In 23 B.C., the poet Horace said, "Seize the day, put no trust in the morrow."</b>
</i><br/><br/><br/>The irony of Horace quote is that Christopher Snow seize the night instead and marvels at it. While everybody slumbers, he prowls the street from dusk 'til dawn. Twenty-eight years old Chris have a Xeroderma-Pigmentosum since birth and no one suspected him to reach adulthood.<br/><br/>In the event of his father's death, Chris doesn't have the time to grieve, he must survive the night and search for the truth. Without fear, h</span>
  <span id="freeText2854479971610080366" style="display:none"><br /><i>
  <b>In 23 B.C., the poet Horace said, "Seize the day, put no trust in the morrow."</b>
</i><br /><br /><br />The irony of Horace quote is that Christopher Snow seize the night instead and marvels at it. While everybody slumbers, he prowls the street from dusk 'til dawn. Twenty-eight years old Chris have a Xeroderma-Pigmentosum since birth and no one suspected him to reach adulthood.<br /><br />In the event of his father's death, Chris doesn't have the time to grieve, he must survive the night and search for the truth. Without fear, he must confront the secret that envelopes his beloved town, Moonlight Bay, because everyone is <i>
  <b>becoming</b>
</i>. A secret no one can escape....<br /><br /><br />A Dean Koontz creation that is worthy to be called <i>
  <b>Action-Thriller</b>
</i>. The tension accelerates at an unrelenting pace and will keep you reading 'til you catch your breath yet again. Even the bucket-full of paraphrases will not overshadow the thrill. Infact, Koontz love for poetry and philosophy made this more interesting. This one captured my attention, so much, that I'm reading the sequel already. I'm hooked!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2854479971610080366" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Pygmy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/406810-pygmy"><img alt="Pygmy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1238598970p2/406810.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/75354387?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pygmy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pygmy" href="/user/show/406810-pygmy">Pygmy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/406810-pygmy?shelf=actionthriller">actionthriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/406810-pygmy?shelf=never_to_finish">never_to_finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/406810-pygmy?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer75354387" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18219635083246217374">The main character has an overly philosophical tone of voice and overuses the word "I" (a common failing in many 1st person POVs, IMO), and many of the characters don't seem to talk very naturally, but it seemed interesting enough, and in terms of evoking a creepy horror feel, Koontz does a decent job. However, halfway through the book, my patience was sorely tried with excessive surfer-lingo that may in fact be accurate, but which to my ears sounded unimaginative, unfunny, and smacked too much </span>
  <span id="freeText18219635083246217374" style="display:none">The main character has an overly philosophical tone of voice and overuses the word "I" (a common failing in many 1st person POVs, IMO), and many of the characters don't seem to talk very naturally, but it seemed interesting enough, and in terms of evoking a creepy horror feel, Koontz does a decent job. However, halfway through the book, my patience was sorely tried with excessive surfer-lingo that may in fact be accurate, but which to my ears sounded unimaginative, unfunny, and smacked too much of Wayne's World or somesuch. After that, I sloughed through paragraphs that excessively described the wonders of pets and their intelligence. I like pets and have one myself, but not nearly enough to want to read pages of it when I want to get back to the thriller/investigation part. Turns out the pets-thing had a point, but it took too long to get to it. Then a predictable shocker scene where a formerly good cop starts blathering about incest-rape fantasies, horror o horror, got bored and I'm not gonna finish.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18219635083246217374" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('r4wSZkONJNMD7r9aKWVZtsoGmaY5t9H0QWroblN/nhMxirmmitSnhlJZhYq9Xb8Vs0Bsl92O/Mx40ufsvDFTOA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Lwqhik8xf/6KSb3JrMprvIvJSPMWccSeHAdiIuH0p2uxDApKhmj8q9v+hxk48o0f8o+9wvJI6aYlv22gDrpqQA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
